From pmvw at outwardfocus.net  Mon Sep 11 21:38:27 2006
From: pmvw at outwardfocus.net (Piet van Weel)
Date: Mon, 11 Sep 2006 20:38:27 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Wireless Networking
In-Reply-To: <e89b36dd0609112127i5264d0c7i2fec2068be63672d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e89b36dd0609102133t2dd6957evd35e107da2dd8de5@mail.gmail.com>	<4504E897.9050004@digitree.org>
	<e89b36dd0609112127i5264d0c7i2fec2068be63672d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <450639C3.6000009@outwardfocus.net>

Try this:

* First, download the windows driver

* Unzip to a directory and remember where you put it.

* Open a terminal window, cd to that directory and run ?ndiswrapper -i 
bcmwl5.inf? as root. This should install configure ndiswrapper to use 
the driver and copy the nessecary files to the right locations.

* run ?ndiswrapper -m? to make the ndiswrapper kernel module load at boot.

* you should now have a ?wlan0? interface that you can configure to fit 
your router config.

Cheers!

Piet

From larry.brigman at gmail.com  Mon Sep 11 21:51:37 2006

Message-ID: <ca5165530609112151s1df4ad5t19e052bf7462c0e5@mail.gmail.com>

lspci is not a directory, it is a command.  It is similar to ls but
for the pci bus.
issue the /sbin/lspci command.  On most system you will get about 1-2 screens
full of information. You will get stuff a lot like this from your system.

02:05.0 Ethernet controller: Digital Equipment Corporation DECchip
21142/43 (rev 41)

Just because the hardware scan doesn't auto-load a driver doesn't mean
it doesn't
know how to handle it.  Wireless on Linux except for the old
orinco/prisum chipsets are typically a trial to get going.  Even then
you have to do a lot of manual configuration.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Tue Sep 12 00:37:18 2006
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Tue, 12 Sep 2006 07:37:18 +0000
Subject: [PLUG] VPN from Mac to Linux
Message-ID: <20060912073718.GA10499@gate.kl-ic.com>


A few weeks ago, I decommissioned my sister's Windows box with
extreme prejudice, ridding the world of one more virus bot.  I
replaced it with a Mac Mini, since I could not talk her into
running Linux.  Sigh.

Now I want to be able to do some admin on the box remotely, without
driving from Beaverton to Gresham.   I admin 2 other Linux boxes
remotely through OpenVPN tunnels drilled from those machines to my
server.

There is an OpenVPN client for Mac OSX, the TUN interface for which
seems to break when Apple upgrades OS-X.  Their "natural" VPN seems
to be a flavor of PPTP (with IPSec?  Not sure, still learning).  The
Mac can also drill a PPP connection over an SSH tunnel, apparently.  
While I don't want to open up more incoming ports on my server,
and support a second protocol for VPN, I also don't want to fight
a mostly-proprietary operating system to keep the connection going
after OS upgrades.

So this is a judgment question, for folks that do this kind of
thing more often:  Which approach is wisest from the reliability
and security standpoint: (1) OpenVPN, (2) PPTP, (3) SSH/PPP ?

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From plug_0 at robinson-west.com  Mon Sep 11 22:50:06 2006
From: plug_0 at robinson-west.com (plug_0 at robinson-west.com)

Subject: [PLUG] Wireless Networking
In-Reply-To: <450639C3.6000009@outwardfocus.net>

Quoting Piet van Weel <pmvw at outwardfocus.net>:

I got a lot of garbage characters, don't know why...

Anyways, is anyone in the wireless ethernet adapter
market flicking Windows support and focusing on OSS
systems directly instead?  USB2 at 400mbps is faster
than 802.11n isn't it?  Is it that hard to make a
USB2 device that's Linux friendly?  I suppose external
scsi is another option, if it's fast enough, to connect
a wireless device to one's computer.  Firewire comes to 
mind, a form of scsi for streaming digital content.

Whether it's madwifi, linuxant, or ndiswrapper: the focus
is on using cards designed for Windows, possibly Mac as 
well, but not Linux under Linux.  The comment about getting 
laughed at when asking for Linux drivers seems like a 
perfectly good reason for someone to start producing 
wireless hardware and specifically target it at the OSS 
community.  What drives the producers of wireless chipsets 
to be proprietary and essentially aligned with Microsoft?  

Microsoft essentially owns all of the successfull proprietary 
OS'es these days, as far as I can tell.  Microsoft may even 
have a controlling interest in MacOS.  Microsoft doesn't 
control Nintendo, Sony, etc., but these are game console 
producers that don't provide real competition to Windows 
and MacOS.

What does it take to convince a hardware manufacturer to produce
a device that anyone can write fully featured GPL'ed drivers for?
Whoever figures out the answer to that question has the potential
to open wireless up substantially for the OSS community.
 
Get away from using arcane virtualization techniques to drive 
wireless hardware, wireless hardware becomes more appropriate for 
applications where reliability is key.  How many expensive mission
critical servers are there these days that rely heavily on wireless 
technology?  Imagine Linux kernel drivers for the latest 
wireless hardware supporting all the latest features that won't 
taint the kernel because they are GPL licensed.  Has anyone released 
hardware drivers for Windows XP under the the GNU general public 
license version 2 or later?

From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Tue Sep 12 09:57:26 2006
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Tue, 12 Sep 2006 09:57:26 -0700

	<Pine.OSX.4.64.0609120743090.5499@arrowhead.galois.com>
Message-ID: <200609120957.26327.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

# from Paul Heinlein
# on Tuesday 12 September 2006 07:44 am:

>> So this is a judgment question, for folks that do this kind of thing
>> more often: ?Which approach is wisest from the reliability and
>> security standpoint: (1) OpenVPN, (2) PPTP, (3) SSH/PPP ?
>
>I'm curious: does standard ssh not meet your needs?

It sounds like Keith might be hoping for a standing incoming connection 
from the mac, which would allow him to initiate an ssh (or maybe also 
vnc) connection from his end.  I haven't tried ssh/ppp on the mac, but 
it has served me well in many other situations.

If the issue is an intermittent network (e.g. dialup), having a standing 
incoming connection whenever the remote box is on is about the only 
answer.  Ditto for firewalls (not that I'm aware of any ISP's that 
block incoming ssh.)

If it is just a matter of dynamic IP, dyndns.com can help you out with a 
free DNS address that can be updated as the IP changes.

--Eric

On Mon, 2006-09-11 at 10:18 -0700, Paul Heinlein wrote:

> In /proc/cpuinfo, the 'flags' section should report 'vmx' if ia32 VT 
> is enabled.

Aaaah, be careful though; CPU flags can lie.  I found out that hard way
recently when I upgraded my workstation.  I assumed that any full P4
w/EMT64 would naturally include Hyperthreading.  The mobo BIOS announced
that HT is enabled when it boots, but for the life of me, I couldn't get
an SMP kernel to recognize more than 1 CPU.

====================================================================
$ cat /proc/cpuinfo
processor       : 0
vendor_id       : GenuineIntel
cpu family      : 15
model           : 4
model name      : Intel(R) Pentium(R) 4 CPU 2.66GHz
stepping        : 9
cpu MHz         : 2660.789
cache size      : 1024 KB
fdiv_bug        : no
hlt_bug         : no
f00f_bug        : no
coma_bug        : no
fpu             : yes
fpu_exception   : yes
cpuid level     : 5
wp              : yes
flags           : fpu vme de pse tsc msr pae mce cx8 apic mtrr pge mca cmov pat pse36 clflush dts acpi mmx fxsr sse sse2 ss ht tm pbe nx lm constant_tsc pni monitor ds_cpl tm2 cid cx16 xtpr
bogomips        : 5327.30
====================================================================

Notice the 'ht'?  Surely it must support Hyperthreading!  Wrong.  The
2.66GHz don't.  I should've spent the $20 more for the 2.8GHz which does
support hyperthreading.

Interestingly, 'x86info' reports:

====================================================================
$ x86info
x86info v1.17.  Dave Jones 2001-2005
Feedback to <davej at redhat.com>.

Found 1 CPU
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Found unknown cache descriptors: 64 81 91 96 112 124
Family: 15 Model: 4 Stepping: 9 Type: 0 Brand: 0
CPU Model: D (Foster)
Processor name string: Intel(R) Pentium(R) 4 CPU 2.66GHz

Feature flags:
 fpu vme de pse tsc msr pae mce cx8 apic sep mtrr pge mca cmov pat pse36 clflsh ds acpi mmx fxsr sse sse2 ss ht tm pbe sse3 monitor ds-cpl tm2 cntx-id cx16 xTPRExtended feature flags:
 xd em64t
Instruction trace cache:
        Size: 12K uOps  8-way associative.
L1 Data cache:
        Size: 16KB      Sectored, 8-way associative.
        line size=64 bytes.
L2 unified cache:
        Size: 1MB       Sectored, 8-way associative.
        line size=64 bytes.
Instruction TLB: 4K, 2MB or 4MB pages, fully associative, 128 entries.
Found unknown cache descriptors: 64 81 91 96 112 124
Data TLB: 4KB or 4MB pages, fully associative, 64 entries.
Processor serial: 0000-0F49-0000-0000-0000-0000
The physical package supports 1 logical processors
====================================================================

On my 3GHz system at work x86info reports:
====================================================================
...
The physical package supports 2 logical processors
====================================================================

But I don't know if really knows or if it's just counting the ones it
finds--a test would a UP kernel or HT disabled would be required to
know.

Hi,

I'm part of the e1000 development team at Intel here in Hillsboro and maybe I 
can help you out (I should hope so, or course). We have a development list for 
e1000 too - see e1000.sf.net and e1000-devel at lists.sourceforge.net.

Can you include the lspci -vv output for me?

I would suggest disabling pciehp - PCI Express Hotplug support in the kernel 
for now, I've seen many problems with it. Double check that your NIC is 
actually inserted correctly into the slot as well.

Also, you should enable MSI support to resolve the shared interrupt issue with 
the adp94xx, hopefully that will help.

Cheers,

Auke

Based on my experience with 64 bit CentOS, I would avoid 64 bit unless
you have a compelling reason for it.  I've been tripped up enough times
by 64 bit issues to make me regret having done a 64 bit install.  No
doubt things are better now than a year ago when I install, but I'd
still think twice before installing 64 bit.

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Tue Sep 12 19:47:53 2006
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Tue, 12 Sep 2006 20:47:53 -0600 (MDT)
Subject: [PLUG] debian net-install media for modern hardware
In-Reply-To: <86odtk4k51.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <86odtk4k51.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0609122028420.9010@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

Ahh, I've been waiting for this... My 64-bit AMD runs sweetly with
gentoo.  There were some issues a year ago, but they have largely
disappeared.  You asked for binaries, so this is not technically an
answer.  But 64-bit gentoo is a strongly viable option.

The only issues still lingering that I personally run into concern video
codecs.  win32codecs is still only available in 32-bit form, which means
you need to use mplayer-bin to view wma files.  This means that
mplayerplug-in for mozilla is not terribly useful for this type of video
file.  With the advent of 64-bit windows, you'd think that win32codecs
will become available in 64-bit form.

My workaround for this is to visit a page with such a video, right-click
and view source, copy the video's link, and then open mplayer-bin in a
shell with the link in the command line.

I guess that those who use their computer for a lot of video-watching
would argue that 64-bit is a pain, but all other uses seem to be well in
hand in gentoo.  Ruby support was a bit behind a year ago, but now it's
right-on.  I once had an issue getting the latest php 5.x, but that was
also a year ago.  Same with mozilla.  OpenOffice simply won't compile on
a 64-bit CPU, but the openoffice-bin package works dandily, and doesn't
take 24 hours to install.

Dunno about your nic.  If you can find a CD distro that can see your
nic, you can use it to install gentoo.  There's no real need to use a
gentoo install CD.  I much prefer to use a knoppix CD for gentoo
installs.

Another bonus: you don't get stuck with a distro kernel.  I really
dislike those.

Carlos Konstanski

On 9/11/06, Larry Brigman <larry.brigman at gmail.com> wrote:
>
> lspci is not a directory, it is a command.  It is similar to ls but
> for the pci bus.
> issue the /sbin/lspci command.  On most system you will get about 1-2
> screens
> full of information. You will get stuff a lot like this from your system.
>
> 02:05.0 Ethernet controller: Digital Equipment Corporation DECchip
> 21142/43 (rev 41)
>
> Just because the hardware scan doesn't auto-load a driver doesn't mean
> it doesn't
> know how to handle it.  Wireless on Linux except for the old
> orinco/prisum chipsets are typically a trial to get going.  Even then
> you have to do a lot of manual configuration.
>
> On 9/11/06, randy.rowlette at gmail.com <randy.rowlette at gmail.com> wrote:

On 9/12/06, randy.rowlette at gmail.com <randy.rowlette at gmail.com> wrote:
> After digging in to my book I find that I answered before researching your
> comments. I do have an output from the sbin/lspci command and it follows.
>...stuff deleted
> 05:02.0 Network controller: Broadcom Corporation BCM4318 [AirForce One 54g]
> 802. 11g Wireless LAN Controller (rev 02)
>... more stuff deleted

So you have a BCM4318 chipset which should work with the newest kernels
2.6.17+
If you are running something older then think about grabbing a copy of
the kernel
tree and building it yourself.

Web site that is did the driver.
http://bcm43xx.berlios.de/

A walk thru on getting it up and running inside ndiswrapper on ubuntu
http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=190177

With fc5 you might just want to plug the laptop into an ethernet connection long
enough to run yum update which should get a later kernel that should
have support
for that chip set.  The cds have a 2.6.15 kernel but the latest update
is 2.6.17.3

Also if you do get it to work read this page and send them the
details. They would
like to know.
http://bcm43xx.berlios.de/?go=Devices

>debian netinst.iso, it
>failed to discover or recognize the intel GigE NIC, which is going to
>make the rest of the net-install a little, er, interesting.

There's been a fair amount of churn lately.  You probably want to grab a 
more modern installer.  While we're talking modern, maybe give the 
memory stick boot a shot:

  http://d-i.alioth.debian.org/manual/en.i386/ch04s04.html

I seem to have zero notes on what I did to get my own stick going, so it 
must have been fairly painless -- well, something about not actually 
need an iso image on it.  I know I did the "hard way" instructions 
because I was using 128MB stick.  IIRC, I grabbed a tarball out of the 
installer maze or maybe mounted an ISO and copied stuff from that.

For extra points, figure out how to add an /etc/hosts entry on the stick 
for your apt-proxy server and report back.

--Eric

Matt,

Matt McKenzie wrote:
> Hey folks-
> 
> I tried to send a fairly big message with some txt dumps right in the
> message body, but it bounced because the mailserv thought it was spam.  So,
> should I attach the dumps as .txt files or will those get rejected too?
> (just some CLI output, and a couple config files).

You can paste text content on the following website, so long as it 
doesn't contain anything "too sensitive".  If you were trying to paste 
it to the PLUG list, which is publicly archived, I would assume there 
wouldn't be anything too bad in it:
http://pastebin.ca/

Pastebin issues you with a URL that you could then paste into the email. 
  You can also do things like password protect it and/or set an expiry date.

From heinlein at madboa.com  Wed Sep 13 05:48:18 2006
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Wed, 13 Sep 2006 05:48:18 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] debian net-install media for modern hardware
In-Reply-To: <86odtk4k51.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <86odtk4k51.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.64.0609130540550.1104@orange.madboa.com>

On Tue, 12 Sep 2006, Russell Senior wrote:

>
> I just got an ASUS p5ld2-vm motherboard and a core 2 duo cpu to go 
> with.  Slapping in my old trusty (crusty?) debian netinst.iso, it 
> failed to discover or recognize the intel GigE NIC, which is going 
> to make the rest of the net-install a little, er, interesting. 
> Knoppix 5.0DVD did a little better.  Oh, and so far neither is 
> particularly liking the video for X11 (at least not on the crufty 
> basement monitor).  Anyone with recent debian install experience 
> with advice on what works best with modern hardware.  I understand 
> these new fangled CPUs do 64bit now too.  Recommendations on 386 vs 
> x86_64 binaries?

Are you using the sarge installer? I've found that etch works and 
plays well with a much broader ranger of hardware. At work, we've got 
some newer machines with Intel 82573L NICs. Etch worked but sarge was 
having no part of it. :-)

As for 32 vs. 64 bits, I've yet to encounter a killer reason for 
loading a 64-bit environment. (That doesn't mean there isn't one; I 
just haven't encountered it.) I run 32-bit kernels and userspace on 
all our Opterons with nothing but good luck.

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> www.madboa.com

Drew,

   It's 1.3.37 (or something close to that).

   Regardless, I figured it out this afternoon; it's one of those
head-slapping situations: so dumb it's embarrassing to let people know about
it.

no included files because the server is not providing the pages. The browser
client is displaying the page. D'oh! As soon as I changed the URL to
http://localhost/appl-ecosys/index.shtml, there were the menus and footer.
Sigh. Just goes to show how infrequently I look at the site locally.

From galens at seitzassoc.com  Thu Sep 14 19:44:32 2006
From: galens at seitzassoc.com (Galen Seitz)
Date: Thu, 14 Sep 2006 19:44:32 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] bug tracking software
Message-ID: <20060915024437.5EB178F00@tinman.seitzassoc.com>


Has anyone here used Mantis(www.mantisbt.org)?  If so, I'd be interested
in hearing your experiences.  I'm trying to determine if it can be
configured appropriately for our business.  I need to be able to track
both hardware and software problems for multiple projects with multiple
clients.  We're not a call center, and clients are unlikely to be
entering or viewing bugs.  The thing that is a little different from 
typical bug tracking needs is the extra level of hierarchy created by
having lots of clients.  I want to be able to separate projects by 
client.  If all projects from all clients were grouped together, it
would eventually get unwieldy.

Bugzilla and scarab appear to be overly complex for my needs.  I've
also briefly looked at gnats, rt, and roundup, but mantis seemed to
be the best fit.

thanks,
galen

From plug at merlot.com  Thu Sep 14 20:27:43 2006
From: plug at merlot.com (Kurt Sussman)
Date: Thu, 14 Sep 2006 20:27:43 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] bug tracking software
In-Reply-To: <20060915024437.5EB178F00@tinman.seitzassoc.com>
References: <20060915024437.5EB178F00@tinman.seitzassoc.com>
Message-ID: <20060915032743.GK32165@merlot.com>

Galen Seitz (galens at seitzassoc.com) typed this ...
> Has anyone here used Mantis(www.mantisbt.org)?  If so, I'd be interested
> in hearing your experiences.  I'm trying to determine if it can be
> configured appropriately for our business.  I need to be able to track
> both hardware and software problems for multiple projects with multiple
> clients.  We're not a call center, and clients are unlikely to be
> entering or viewing bugs.  The thing that is a little different from 
> typical bug tracking needs is the extra level of hierarchy created by
> having lots of clients.  I want to be able to separate projects by 
> client.  If all projects from all clients were grouped together, it
> would eventually get unwieldy.

I patched Mantis to allow multiple subdomains, each with its own
database. The main codebase is shared, but none of the data. Do you need
to run aggregate reports, or are per-client reports OK? If the subdomain
separation is something you might like, I'll send you the patch. I think
it's about 12 lines.

If you're saying that you want each client-project pair to have its own
distinct list of bugs, I'm sure you could do that with clever project
and version list configuration.

> Bugzilla and scarab appear to be overly complex for my needs.  I've
> also briefly looked at gnats, rt, and roundup, but mantis seemed to
> be the best fit.

Mantis is a really nice bug tracker.

As Dr. Shepard suggested, Trac is great for integrating a wiki, bug
tracking, and Subversion. Mantis is just a bug tracker.

--Kurt

    Merlot Research Group, Inc               http://www.merlot.com

The wpa_supplicant daemon doesn't just support just the Host AP wireless 
driver. I guess the mailing list name is a bit confusing though. I use the 
wpa_supplicant daemon to get WPA-PSK to work on my laptop which uses the 
Intel ipw2200 driver.

From sparkey7 at gmail.com  Fri Sep 15 10:00:33 2006

Subject: [PLUG] Minicom Help Please!
Message-ID: <ee892c770609151000m14f2a614r1327ee4719149068@mail.gmail.com>

Hello All,

I just got Minicom up and running sucesfully for console access into cisco
routers. I want to know if there is a way to use a "cut and paste" feature
within the program?

There is sometimes a need, if an interface goes down, to cut the config from
the bad interface, and paste it to an available one.

Or, is there another hyperterminal program people prefer. FYI, I am running
knoppix locally on a toshiba laptop.

Thanks for any help

Joe

Joe,

Joe Langley wrote:
> Hello All,
> 
> I just got Minicom up and running sucesfully for console access into cisco
> routers. I want to know if there is a way to use a "cut and paste" feature
> within the program?

Are you running minicom from within a terminal in the X window manager 
or just standard terminals (ie. <ctrl>+<alt>+<f1>)?  If you're in X, 
doesn't highlighting the source text with the mouse and then 
middle-clicking in the destination window work?

If you need to maintain certain word-wrap properties, you can make a 
capture/log file of all communications in minicom by using the "-C 
<filename>" option and then use a program like gedit or kedit to 
highlight the source text?

Cheers,

Daniel Hedlund

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Fri Sep 15 18:39:16 2006
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Fri, 15 Sep 2006 19:39:16 -0600 (MDT)
Subject: [PLUG] PCMCIA CF / SD card reader suggestions?
In-Reply-To: <86d59xc5nm.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <c834ec80609110904h7e5c7771l8685a78bba4167c0@mail.gmail.com>
	<2e42bd9b0609111818r532fa45fhab5613ceb4638bce@mail.gmail.com>
	<55cf303a0609151018p76fda3b6mfd51406ee75adfab@mail.gmail.com>
	<450AE43A.3090503@foo-projects.org> <86d59xc5nm.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0609151931420.13931@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

My multi-slot reader requires a certain kernel config parameter set
to "Y" to allow access to all the SCSI devices:

CONFIG_SCSI_MULTI_LUN:

If you have a SCSI device that supports more than one LUN (Logical
Unit Number), e.g. a CD jukebox, and only one LUN is detected, you
can say Y here to force the SCSI driver to probe for multiple LUNs.
A SCSI device with multiple LUNs acts logically like multiple SCSI
devices. The vast majority of SCSI devices have only one LUN, and
so most people can say N here. The max_luns boot/module parameter
allows to override this setting.

Symbol: SCSI_MULTI_LUN [=y]
Prompt: Probe all LUNs on each SCSI device
   Defined at drivers/scsi/Kconfig:167
   Depends on: SCSI
   Location:
     -> Device Drivers
       -> SCSI device support
         -> SCSI device support (SCSI [=y])

Carlos Konstanski

From alan at clueserver.org  Fri Sep 15 22:37:16 2006
From: alan at clueserver.org (Alan)
Date: Fri, 15 Sep 2006 22:37:16 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] PLUG Advanced Topics September 18th 2006
Message-ID: <1158385036.3834.6.camel@zowie.fnordora.org>

September 2006 Portland Linux/Unix Group Advanced topics meeting 

Speaker: Ted Kubaska

Topic:   introduction to Eclipse 3.2

This talk is an introduction to Eclipse 3.2. It assumes that you know
what Eclipse is and may even have installed it and cruised its menus,
that you have not done anything serious with it, but that you might want
to. Eclipse is both an IDE and an RCP (a starting platform for your own
applications). Although I'll mention and define RCP, the talk is about
using Eclipse as an IDE. I'll show how to use Eclipse to build a simple
Java console application. As an IDE, it allows you to add your own
plug-ins. The talk will also show how to add a simple plug-in. This talk
is cribbed from various books; little if any of it is original.

Time: 
        7pm until 9pm or so. ***NOTE*** There is a party before us that ends at 7pm, so we may start a bit late.

Date: 
        Monday September 18th 2006

Location:
        Jax [Restaurant]
        826 SW 2nd Ave
        Portland, OR

        On the MAX Line, next to Bally's Fitness.  This is one block  
up and over from Paddy's.

This is a bit late, but then I'm way behind on a bunch of things.  
Anyway, just 'cause no one mentioned it, the Ars Technica system guide 
is a good place to look for ideas, tips, and inspiration on building 
your own system.  Ars divides its guide into three categories (Budget 
Box, Hot Rod Box, and God Box) and updates it frequently, the most 
recent update being last month.  I like checking it out regardless of 
whether I'm shopping for anything, simply because it's interesting to 
see what's out there, what's considered cutting-edge or hot, what's 
considered solid and a good value, and so on.  The comments are usually 
worth checking out also.

http://arstechnica.com/guides.ars

From heinlein at madboa.com  Sat Sep 16 10:01:10 2006
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Sat, 16 Sep 2006 10:01:10 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Forcing Gentoo package check
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.64.0609160924570.6251@orange.madboa.com>

Some time ago, I'd begun to think that perhaps the Gentoo package 
system on my SPARC had become somewhat corrupted. (Snip long story 
about SunBlades and IDE corruption...) Queries concerning installed 
packages seemed to execute correctly, but "emerge -uvD world" seemed 
to ignore packages that really needed to be upgraded.

I finally got around to brute-forcing the portage system into querying 
every single installed package to see if it was in need of an update. 
The resulting pipe sequence is convoluted and takes a while to run, 
but it seems to do the job. Oh, and you'll also need to have the epm 
ebuild installed.

   epm -qGa |\
   sed -e 's/-r[0-9][0-9]*$//' -e 's/-[^-]*$//' |\
   sort -u |\
   (while read n; do emerge -puv "$n"; done) |\
   grep -w ebuild

In semi-plain English, the procedure is

1. Get list of all installed ebuilds, complete with group name
2. Remove release and version numbers from ebuild names
3. Remove duplicates, common with slotted ebuilds
4. Loop over each ebuild name looking for updates
5. Important output from emerge has word "ebuild" in the string

It's unlikely that this will help anyone else, but who knows? :-)

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> www.madboa.com

the list directly to emerge instead of invoking it each time.

For resolving, portage has to load up the old style virtuals- to do 
this, it has to walk the entire vdb, so your scriptlet above is in 
effect a N^2 walk of the vdb (ouch).

Depending on how many packages you have, you might be better off doing

emerge --sync; emerge -ev world

which essentially figures out the whole dependency tree and recompiles
everything from the leaves up to the root. With all the stuff I have installed,
it takes about 48 hours on a 933 MHz Pentium.

Incidentally, if you haven't bitten the gcc 4 bullet, you'll end up recompiling
everything anyhow, so there's no good reason to do it *twice*!


From ferringb at gmail.com  Sat Sep 16 21:06:22 2006

Message-ID: <20060917040622.GA6835@seldon>

On Sat, Sep 16, 2006 at 11:38:33PM -0400, znmeb at cesmail.net wrote:
> Quoting Brian Harring <ferringb at gmail.com>:
> > Won't pick up slotted updates offhand; also, I'd personally just feed
> > the list directly to emerge instead of invoking it each time.
> >
> > For resolving, portage has to load up the old style virtuals- to do
> > this, it has to walk the entire vdb, so your scriptlet above is in
> > effect a N^2 walk of the vdb (ouch).

> > ~harring
> 
> Depending on how many packages you have, you might be better off doing
> 
> emerge --sync; emerge -ev world
> 
> which essentially figures out the whole dependency tree and recompiles
> everything from the leaves up to the root.

Leaves being defined as what is in world; it's actually _not_ every 
package on the system, since you can have packages not in world 
(emerge --oneshot or ebuild /path/to/ebuild usage), or have the 
resultant 'empty' graph from the tree no longer including nodes in 
the vdb.

Example of the latter would be that you had pkg x-1 merged which 
needed y, x-2 no longer needs y thus y doesn't show up in the graph 
unless you've forced it into the world file yourself.

~harring

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Sat Sep 16 21:23:00 2006
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Sat, 16 Sep 2006 22:23:00 -0600 (MDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Forcing Gentoo package check
In-Reply-To: <20060916233833.t2ptdlc8w048ko4c@webmail.spamcop.net>
References: <Pine.OSX.4.64.0609160924570.6251@orange.madboa.com>
	<20060917010253.GA6163@seldon>
	<20060916233833.t2ptdlc8w048ko4c@webmail.spamcop.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0609162152230.12289@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

What about system packages?  Does "emerge -ev world" get these?

root at sphinktoo:/var/lib/portage# emerge -ep system |wc
     259    1038   11171
root at sphinktoo:/var/lib/portage# emerge -ep `cat /var/lib/portage/world` |wc
    1061    4258   47724
root at sphinktoo:/var/lib/portage# emerge -ep world |wc
    1071    4299   48068

Judging from this output, "emerge -e world" gets a little bit of stuff
that "emerge -e `cat /var/lib/portage/world`" does not.  It would take
some sifting to identify the missing 10 packages.

The output from both these emerge world variants do indeed contain
enough system packages to imply that they do, in fact, get them.
module-init-tools, file, busybox and others are in the mix.

I'm throwing the `cat world` method out there because it is a way to
re-create a gentoo box with all the packages of another gentoo box.
Once the base system is built, you can copy the first system's world
file to the second system and run the emerge command.  When I hosed my
dev workstation, I backed up my data and world file and used this
method to re-create the load from a fresh build.  The result was
pleasantly identical to the original (but without the hose-factor).

I have always wondered how to do this on a debian (apt-based) system.
Anyone know?  I switched to gentoo before getting to the bottom of it.

But for the usual repair jobs, "emerge -e world" has the slight edge,
winning by 10 packages on my system.

Carlos Konstanski

From creswick at gmail.com  Sun Sep 17 12:46:15 2006
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Sun, 17 Sep 2006 12:46:15 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] emule site problems...
In-Reply-To: <1158510050.450d75e204a40@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
References: <1158510050.450d75e204a40@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <c834ec80609171246h753c5daavfd5c40fc9d06c62@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/17/06, plug_0 at robinson-west.com <plug_0 at robinson-west.com> wrote:
> http://content.emule-project.net/view.php?pid=1519
>
> I can't figure out how to get Freedos 1.0 under Fedora Core 5 using this site.
> It requires a special downloader.

Yeah.. it requires an eDonkey client (hence the ed2k:// uri..), of
which eMule is one of many, and it appears that eMule is windows-only.

> There don't appear to be any instructions
> to compile this downloader under Linux let alone any rpm releases, which is
> strange considering that the software is supposedly GPL'ed.  It's irritating
> that MS Windows systems are the only ones listed as compatible platforms.
> MacOS-X doesn't even appear to be listed as a compatible platform.

There is *nothing* about the GPL which requires (or even suggests)
multi-OS releases.  Porting is a lot of work, especially if you don't
personally use the platform you're porting to.

> What is wrong with the standard methods of downloading large software packages
> that have made the e-mule downloader necessary?

Bandwith.  eMule is one of a number of peer-to-peer networking clients
that allow the bandwith hit to be spread across many voulnteer
connections.  The groups that create and (initially) host projects
such as freedos or other distros have to pay for their bandwith usage
some how, and since they aren't making loads of cash through the
effort of compiling these tools / OSes, they've wisely opted for a
distribution mechanism that most people are perfectly happy with,
often produces faster download speeds, is far more robust, and it's
much, much cheaper.


> What is up with me not being to download a copy of Freedos 1.0 from ibiblio
> without corrupting it?  Lately, I can't even start a download from ibiblio.
> It is as if I got blacklisted.

No idea...

From ehem at m5p.com  Sun Sep 17 13:26:28 2006
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Sun, 17 Sep 2006 13:26:28 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Forcing Gentoo package check
In-Reply-To: <20060917173117.AB6FD45D9@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200609172026.k8HKQTcV045373@m5p.com>

>From: Carlos Konstanski <ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com>
> I have always wondered how to do this on a debian (apt-based) system.
> Anyone know?  I switched to gentoo before getting to the bottom of it.

I think there is more to it, but `dpkg --get-selections` (or the reverse
--set-selections) is most of the equivalent. I think there is more data
hiding in `aptitude`, but the above will at least get you the package
manager's view. You can also get debconf settings with
`debconf-get-selections`.

	<1158449710.450c8a2eb6414@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <450E0ECB.8070002@telestream.com>

plug_0 at robinson-west.com wrote:

> It's a shame that almost every
> retail computer with Windows preinstalled is an OEM installation.  The biggest
> problem with an OEM copy of Windows is that NOONE TAKES RESPONSIBILITY FOR 
> SUPPORTING IT, INCLUDING THE INSTALLER.  This is especially true with Fry's.

This has nothing to do with MS.  This is a retailer gripe.

> My definition of the God machine is one that lets you do with Linux everything
> you thought only Windows or MacOS-X could do and more that you like but never
> knew about.  It's a cheap cop out to give advice on building a great Windows
> system.  All IBM PC compatible computer hardware is designed for Windows and
> Windows only.  No matter how hot a Windows or MacOSX system is, the
> owner of that system is still trapped in EULA hell if they don't switch to
> either Linux or FreeBSD.

This is not very accurate.  Linux and BSD don't have drivers for 
everything not because of MS, but in most cases because of other patent 
or IP reasons.  MS pays for a lot of their features, which in turn is 
paid for by us.  Take Linspire for example, or any other pay-for version 
of a Linux based OS that is able to play DVD's and MP3's out of the box. 
  They're not free technologies.  It's why a lot of gaming consoles that 
play DVD's require an extra dongle.  You're buying the right to play it, 
and it kept the cost of the original equipment down.

-- 
- m0gely

September 2006 Portland Linux/Unix Group Advanced topics meeting

Speaker: Ted Kubaska

Topic:   introduction to Eclipse 3.2

This talk is an introduction to Eclipse 3.2. It assumes that you know
what Eclipse is and may even have installed it and cruised its menus,
that you have not done anything serious with it, but that you might want
to. Eclipse is both an IDE and an RCP (a starting platform for your own
applications). Although I'll mention and define RCP, the talk is about
using Eclipse as an IDE. I'll show how to use Eclipse to build a simple
Java console application. As an IDE, it allows you to add your own
plug-ins. The talk will also show how to add a simple plug-in. This talk
is cribbed from various books; little if any of it is original.

From ehem at m5p.com  Mon Sep 18 22:20:18 2006
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Mon, 18 Sep 2006 22:20:18 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Possibly OT Laptop hardware question...
In-Reply-To: <20060918190005.5F87745DC@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200609190520.k8J5KIwn064573@m5p.com>

>From: Chris Penwell <romanmir_ug at comcast.net>
> When I unplug the laptop, I want it to fall into hibernate; which I am
> pretty sure can be handled through software. When I plug it in, however,
> I want it to pop back up from hibernate without any intervention (or as
> little as possible..)
> 
> Does such a beast exist? Or am I gonna hafta to babysit the dumb thing?
> 
> If this is OT, any pointers in the right direction would be
> appreciated... TIA.

I'm pretty sure you can solve the first part via ACPI support. I think it
would amount to placing a script in /etc/acpi/events/<something> which
gets executed when AC power is removed. I'm pretty sure the kernel will
see this, and you'd need a pretty simple script to make it hibernate.

The wakeup is trickier. It might involve going into the BIOS and telling
it to wakeup on power restoration. There /might/ also be a way to do this
via ACPI, but I don't know where to start besides ACPI.

From eli.stair at gmail.com  Tue Sep 19 08:47:23 2006
From: eli.stair at gmail.com (Eli Stair)
Date: Tue, 19 Sep 2006 08:47:23 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] route-ethX format ( Redhat-ian distributions )
In-Reply-To: <45100130.1040700@acm.org>
References: <45100130.1040700@acm.org>
Message-ID: <f4468cae0609190847u6381cf2fm3018da1c2580840f@mail.gmail.com>

Don't know which examples you've found not to work for you, but these
are the two I've known to work:

10.65.42.0/25 via 10.65.42.126 dev eth0

GATEWAY0=10.65.42.126
NETMASK0=255.255.255.128
ADDRESS0=10.65.42.0

Quick snip from some notes, IIRC the latter version is the
current-used format in RHEL4*.  Check the network-functions and
ifup/ifdown scripts to see what's currently sourced from the
route-${INT} files and used to create static routes.

/eli

From creswick at gmail.com  Wed Sep 20 10:23:37 2006
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Wed, 20 Sep 2006 10:23:37 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Two screen presentation software
In-Reply-To: <7DF864D22974394599201D05DFA26668019106F9@marlin.csuci.edu>
References: <7DF864D22974394599201D05DFA26668019106F9@marlin.csuci.edu>
Message-ID: <c834ec80609201023gbbf11c2n26d9416209e61df1@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/20/06, Garcia, Jorge <jorge.garcia at csuci.edu> wrote:
>  I have tried several things and none works so far, I see in both
> monitors, in full screen,
>  the same output, even when I change the display setting and I
>  choose monitor one (my computer one) to be the default one and
>  I choose monitor two (the wall screen) to extend my windows desktop
> onto this monitor.

If running linux, you could run separate x-servers on each monitor.
Then you will be able to run acrobat in full-screen on the wall while
still using your other screen for notes or whatever.  This does,
however, make it a little difficult to controll the acroread session
(you can pan over with the mouse, of course).  Running a vnc server on
the wall screen X server will let you vnc into it from the "private"
monitor, which would work great if the wall screen is running at a
significantly lower res. than your private screen, even if not, you
could probably deal with it.

HTH,
--Rogan

>  I wonder if somebody knows something about the configuration of the
> projector or the monitors or the settings

From doug at mindglow.net  Tue Sep 19 08:44:57 2006
From: doug at mindglow.net (Doug Davis)
Date: Tue, 19 Sep 2006 11:44:57 -0400 (EDT)
Subject: [PLUG] route-ethX format ( Redhat-ian distributions )
In-Reply-To: <45100130.1040700@acm.org>
References: <45100130.1040700@acm.org>
Message-ID: <35570.208.253.107.134.1158680697.squirrel@www.geekisp.com>


>
> Can anyone provide a example of how to route all traffic for the
> 192.168.0.0 network through eth2?  I'm pretty sure I can sort out the
> other two from.  :-)
>
>
Add the following to /etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/route-eth2

GATEWAY0=10.10.0.1 #IP for your eth2 gateway
NETMASK0=255.255.255.0 # netmask for your 192.168.0.0 network
ADDRESS0=192.168.0.0

# These are arrays, so the second set is 1, thrid set is 2, etc.
GATEWAY1=10.10.0.1
NETMASK1=255.255.0.0
ADDRESS1=10.0.0.0

Then you need to restart your network by doing a service network restart.


Hope that helps.

Doug Davis


From drew.wymore at gmail.com  Thu Sep 21 11:27:44 2006
From: drew.wymore at gmail.com (drew wymore)
Date: Thu, 21 Sep 2006 11:27:44 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] debugging hyperthreading problems
Message-ID: <e2aeccd60609211127r29cc48c2hceacb914db55898@mail.gmail.com>

Hey All-
I have a Dell 1425SC with a 2.8 Ghz Xeon when I have hyperthreading enabled
if a user initiates a ssh or telnet (I used telnet for testing only) session
and they have bash as their default shell they have to type characters
several times before they output to their terminal program (ie putty). If I
disable hyperthreading or turn off the second CPU in
/sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu1/online using the kernel hotplug feature
everything acts as it should (no having to repeat characters).

I've ruled out a global profile type issue I believe as when I change the
user to tcsh for instance the issue doesn't show itself. I have recompiled
bash thinking that may have been the issue and I'm still seeing though. I
have upgraded to kernel 2.6.18 with same result. I also thought that perhaps
it might be due to LDAP auth but I added a local shadow passwd user and they
show the same problems as LDAP authenticated users.

Anyone have any ideas?

Thanks,
Drew-

From heinlein at madboa.com  Thu Sep 21 11:44:38 2006
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Thu, 21 Sep 2006 11:44:38 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] debugging hyperthreading problems
In-Reply-To: <e2aeccd60609211127r29cc48c2hceacb914db55898@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e2aeccd60609211127r29cc48c2hceacb914db55898@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.64.0609211139480.1043@arrowhead.galois.com>

On Thu, 21 Sep 2006, drew wymore wrote:

> I have a Dell 1425SC with a 2.8 Ghz Xeon when I have hyperthreading 
> enabled if a user initiates a ssh or telnet (I used telnet for 
> testing only) session and they have bash as their default shell they 
> have to type characters several times before they output to their 
> terminal program (ie putty). If I disable hyperthreading or turn off 
> the second CPU in /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu1/online using the 
> kernel hotplug feature everything acts as it should (no having to 
> repeat characters).
> 
> I've ruled out a global profile type issue I believe as when I 
> change the user to tcsh for instance the issue doesn't show itself. 
> I have recompiled bash thinking that may have been the issue and I'm 
> still seeing though. I have upgraded to kernel 2.6.18 with same 
> result. I also thought that perhaps it might be due to LDAP auth but 
> I added a local shadow passwd user and they show the same problems 
> as LDAP authenticated users.
> 
> Anyone have any ideas?

On the Dell, try running sshd in debug, no-fork mode on an alternative 
port:

  /usr/sbin/sshd -d -f /etc/ssh/sshd_config -p 2222

Have the remote user launch a session (using port 2222, or whatever) 
while you keep an eye on the sshd debug output. It may help to add 
extra -d's (-dd or -ddd) to increase verbosity.

You might also try wrapping the debug sshd in strace to catch errant 
system calls:

  strace -o /tmp/sshd.trace /usr/bin/sshd -d [...]

After the session, peek at the sshd.trace file to see if anything 
leaps out.

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> www.madboa.com

On 9/21/06, Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com> wrote:
>
> On Thu, 21 Sep 2006, drew wymore wrote:
>
> > I have a Dell 1425SC with a 2.8 Ghz Xeon when I have hyperthreading
> > enabled if a user initiates a ssh or telnet (I used telnet for
> > testing only) session and they have bash as their default shell they
> > have to type characters several times before they output to their
> > terminal program (ie putty). If I disable hyperthreading or turn off
> > the second CPU in /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu1/online using the
> > kernel hotplug feature everything acts as it should (no having to
> > repeat characters).
> >
> > I've ruled out a global profile type issue I believe as when I
> > change the user to tcsh for instance the issue doesn't show itself.
> > I have recompiled bash thinking that may have been the issue and I'm
> > still seeing though. I have upgraded to kernel 2.6.18 with same
> > result. I also thought that perhaps it might be due to LDAP auth but
> > I added a local shadow passwd user and they show the same problems
> > as LDAP authenticated users.
> >
> > Anyone have any ideas?
>
> On the Dell, try running sshd in debug, no-fork mode on an alternative
> port:
>
>   /usr/sbin/sshd -d -f /etc/ssh/sshd_config -p 2222
>
> Have the remote user launch a session (using port 2222, or whatever)
> while you keep an eye on the sshd debug output. It may help to add
> extra -d's (-dd or -ddd) to increase verbosity.
>
> You might also try wrapping the debug sshd in strace to catch errant
> system calls:
>
>   strace -o /tmp/sshd.trace /usr/bin/sshd -d [...]
>
> After the session, peek at the sshd.trace file to see if anything
> leaps out.
>
> --
> Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> www.madboa.com
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug
>


From raanders at acm.org  Fri Sep 22 10:13:04 2006
From: raanders at acm.org (Roderick A. Anderson)
Date: Fri, 22 Sep 2006 10:13:04 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] route-ethX format ( Redhat-ian distributions )
In-Reply-To: <35570.208.253.107.134.1158680697.squirrel@www.geekisp.com>
References: <45100130.1040700@acm.org>
	<35570.208.253.107.134.1158680697.squirrel@www.geekisp.com>
Message-ID: <451419A0.7010100@acm.org>

Doug Davis wrote:
>>Can anyone provide a example of how to route all traffic for the
>>192.168.0.0 network through eth2?  I'm pretty sure I can sort out the
>>other two from.  :-)
>>
>>
> 
> Add the following to /etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/route-eth2
> 
> GATEWAY0=10.10.0.1 #IP for your eth2 gateway
> NETMASK0=255.255.255.0 # netmask for your 192.168.0.0 network
> ADDRESS0=192.168.0.0
> 
> # These are arrays, so the second set is 1, thrid set is 2, etc.
> GATEWAY1=10.10.0.1
> NETMASK1=255.255.0.0
> ADDRESS1=10.0.0.0

Thanks Doug.  This is very clear.


Rod
-- 
> 
> Then you need to restart your network by doing a service network restart.
> 
> 
> Hope that helps.
> 
> Doug Davis
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug

From johnxj at comcast.net  Fri Sep 22 12:55:01 2006
From: johnxj at comcast.net (John Jordan)
Date: Fri, 22 Sep 2006 12:55:01 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Locked out again :(
Message-ID: <4513DD25.3730.5E4B95D4@localhost>

I was trying to use rsync to copy everything on my laptop's Ubuntu-64 
partition (hda2 -- hda1 is a swap partition) to an external 60 GB USB disk. 
Rsync appeared to do the job, but it ended with an error that the disk was 
out of space. The USB disk had lots of space, but I also got several 
popups in the corner of the screen that I was running out of disk space. In 
other words, evidently it was hda2 that was running out of space, not the 
USB disk. I don't understand that, as all rsync should be doing is reading 
the files on hda2. 

When rsync finished I discovered that the keyboard and mouse were 
locked up. I had no choice but to hit the power button. When I restarted I 
got the following error message when I tried to log in: 

"GDM could not write to your authorization file. This could mean that you 
are out of disk space or that your home directory could not be opened for 
writing. In any event, it is not possible to log in. Please contact your 
system administrator." 

I used Ctrl-Alt-F1 to exit to a shell, whereupon I logged in and then deleted 
a number of large files that I knew I had backups of elsewhere -- about 300 
MB worth. Then I went back to the login screen and tried to log in again. 
But I still got the same error message. 


I went back to the shell and did "sudo chown jjj:jjj /home", thinking that 
perhaps permissions had gotten screwed up. The command executed 
normally, but I still cannot log in. 


A possible part of the problem: There appears to be a file or folder (colors 
are not working in the shell) named "--exclude=media." This was part of the 
rsync command I used. I have tried to remove this file or folder, but I cannot 
do so. 


This is all part of a previous problem where I created a hard link between 
hda2 and hda3. Before trying some ideas to resolve that problem I am 
trying to make a complete backup of each partition. I did succeed in using 
kdar to back up /home, but kdar takes forever to configure. In other words, 
using it to back up other folders or the whole partition is not trivial. Plus, it 
is very unstable -- locks up the computer 50% of the time. I tried using cp, 
but it cannot take an --exclude command, so it tries to copy everything on 
/media/usbdisk, while copying to the usbdisk! I also tried tar, but getting 
the --exclude switch to work with tar is beyond me. I can get it to work with 
rsync, but the same syntax does not work with tar, even though the 
documentation shows it as the same. 


Currently I am stuck having to write this on a Windows desktop because I 
can't get into my Linux computer! I really need suggestions! 


From johnxj at comcast.net  Fri Sep 22 12:57:49 2006
From: johnxj at comcast.net (John Jason Jordan)
Date: Fri, 22 Sep 2006 12:57:49 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Locked out again :(
In-Reply-To: <4513DD25.3730.5E4B95D4@localhost>
References: <4513DD25.3730.5E4B95D4@localhost>
Message-ID: <20060922125749.8f59f5ef.johnxj@comcast.net>

On Fri, 22 Sep 2006 12:55:01 -0700
"John Jordan" <johnxj at comcast.net> dijo:

Never mind. It should have let me in once I had 300 MB free, but I went
back and discovered something else. When I used rsync I told it to
rsync to a folder on the usbdisk. Unfortunately, I must have left
something out of the command because it rsynced everything
to /media/usbdisk, not to the physical disk. So the disk really was
full. So I (very scary for a command line newbie here) removed the
rsynced stuff from /media, and finally was able to log in.

Now, back to the drawing board. <sigh>

> back and discovered something else. When I used rsync I told it to
> rsync to a folder on the usbdisk. Unfortunately, I must have left
> something out of the command because it rsynced everything
> to /media/usbdisk, not to the physical disk. So the disk really was
> full. So I (very scary for a command line newbie here) removed the
> rsynced stuff from /media, and finally was able to log in.
> 
> Now, back to the drawing board. <sigh>

How about '-n' (or '--dry-run') to preview what's going to happen?

Wil

From rsteff at comcast.net  Fri Sep 22 15:49:51 2006
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Fri, 22 Sep 2006 15:49:51 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Newly assembled machine overheating
Message-ID: <4514688F.60405@comcast.net>

I have an overheating processor chip (thank you chip and mother board 
makers for adding temperature sensing and alarms) and need some ideas on 
what might be causing the problem.

I've just assembled a machine:

Soyo IT600 Dragon Ultra mother board with an AMD Athlon XP 2200+ 
processor and a thermaltake Silent Boost chip fan. I used thermal 
grease. The mother board was slightly used, with a different chip, by a 
fellow PLUGer. My processor chip is new, from Computer Geeks.

After checking all the connections, I fired up the machine and got the 
mother board splash screen, hit <DEL> and got into the BIOS. I went 
through the list and found most everything OK the way it was -- I just 
re-ordered the boot sequence (CD-ROM first, Floppy second, HDD, third) 
and disabled the splash screen so I could see what's going on under the 
hood.

That worked fine, and I could see the CPU temperature and the fact that 
the alarm was enabled so I'd know when to start worrying about the CPU 
getting too hot.

It took a fairly long time to finally get around to booting, but 
eventually the SuSE 10.1 install CD booted. I entered the FTP site and 
waited another fairly long time for the process to begin. Just as it 
did, the alarm went off. I aborted the installation and rebooted. The 
processor chip temperature was 44deg C. I recall that the limit is 45, 
so I shut down the machine.

I set the box up on the desk, took the cover off, power it up and 
watched to see if the CPU fan was running: it was, as was the chip set 
fan, the power supply fan, and the two additional case fans.

The only unusual thing that occurred during assembly was that when I 
poked a little hole in the thermal grease packet I must have made two 
holes, one front and one back. I watched a small amount of grease come 
out the front hole, but didn't see about twice as much come out the 
back. The extra grease ran off the chip top and down onto the chip's 
carrier board. There are some little bumps of something that are next to 
the chip top. The grease got on and in between those. I used a q-tip to 
clean up most of it. I was sure to leave grease on the chip top, but I 
don't really know how much there should be.

Any recommendations on what to do next?

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens



From galens at seitzassoc.com  Fri Sep 22 16:22:12 2006

Richard C. Steffens <rsteff at comcast.net> wrote:

> It took a fairly long time to finally get around to booting, but
> eventually the SuSE 10.1 install CD booted. I entered the FTP site and
> waited another fairly long time for the process to begin. Just as it
> did, the alarm went off. I aborted the installation and rebooted. The
> processor chip temperature was 44deg C. I recall that the limit is 45,
> so I shut down the machine.

Assuming that the 45 degree temperature is at the chip, that's not
very hot at all.  For example, the max die temperature for the 
XP Processor Model 10 with 256K L2 Cache is 85 degrees C for the 2200+
model.  BTW, I can tell you from personal experience that an IC
package at 90 degrees C will burn your finger.

> The only unusual thing that occurred during assembly was that when I
> poked a little hole in the thermal grease packet I must have made two
> holes, one front and one back. I watched a small amount of grease come
> out the front hole, but didn't see about twice as much come out the
> back. The extra grease ran off the chip top and down onto the chip's
> carrier board. There are some little bumps of something that are next
> to the chip top. The grease got on and in between those. I used a
> q-tip to clean up most of it. I was sure to leave grease on the chip
> top, but I don't really know how much there should be.

The bumps are most likely decoupling capacitors.  I doubt you caused a
problem with the extra grease.  

> 
> Any recommendations on what to do next?

Double check your alarm settings.  45 degrees C is too low for a chip
overtemperature alarm.


galen

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Fri Sep 22 20:17:46 2006
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Fri, 22 Sep 2006 20:17:46 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Newly assembled machine overheating
In-Reply-To: <4514688F.60405@comcast.net>
References: <4514688F.60405@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <20060923031746.GA14083@gate.kl-ic.com>

On Fri, Sep 22, 2006 at 03:49:51PM -0700, Richard C. Steffens wrote:
> I have an overheating processor chip (thank you chip and mother board 
> makers for adding temperature sensing and alarms) and need some ideas on 
> what might be causing the problem.
> 
> I've just assembled a machine:
...
> That worked fine, and I could see the CPU temperature and the fact that 
> the alarm was enabled so I'd know when to start worrying about the CPU 
> getting too hot.
> 
> It took a fairly long time to finally get around to booting, but 
> eventually the SuSE 10.1 install CD booted. I entered the FTP site and 
> waited another fairly long time for the process to begin. Just as it 
> did, the alarm went off. I aborted the installation and rebooted. The 
> processor chip temperature was 44deg C. I recall that the limit is 45, 
> so I shut down the machine.
...

If the processor is getting very hot, then the heat sink should be
getting quite hot, too.  If it is not, then there is something blocking
the heat flow to the heat sink, for example a plastic film that is
supposed to be removed to expose a thermally conductive soft plastic.
Or the heat sink isn't properly anchored.  Or you have the wrong kind
of heat sink for your processor.  Or the processor voltage is too high
(check the BIOS for voltages, compare that to the processor type you
have).  Or the motherboard is bad.  Or the processor is bad.  Or ...?

I had a similar overheating problem with my wife's Shuttle ATX.  It
turned out to be a failed fan control on the motherboard.  Fortunately,
there was a second socket for the fan, so I just moved the fan plug to
that second socket.  

Some motherboards have all sorts of controls over fan speed in the BIOS.
Record the current fan settings (so you can restore them), then set the
fans to "high speed all the time".  If they still move slowly, that is
one problem, if they move fast but the chip still gets hot, then it
is probably the heat sink interface, or something not working.

It is a pity that most motherboards don't measure processor CURRENT.
That would tell you if something was broken in the CPU or on your
motherboard.  Still, if the voltage is too LOW, it could indicate
a problem with overcurrent.

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs


From ehem at m5p.com  Fri Sep 22 20:33:01 2006
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Fri, 22 Sep 2006 20:33:01 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Newly assembled machine overheating
In-Reply-To: <20060923010733.B7CDD46FD@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200609230333.k8N3X1po006731@m5p.com>

>From: "Richard C. Steffens" <rsteff at comcast.net>
> The only unusual thing that occurred during assembly was that when I 
> poked a little hole in the thermal grease packet I must have made two 
> holes, one front and one back. I watched a small amount of grease come 
> out the front hole, but didn't see about twice as much come out the 
> back. The extra grease ran off the chip top and down onto the chip's 
> carrier board. There are some little bumps of something that are next to 
> the chip top. The grease got on and in between those. I used a q-tip to 
> clean up most of it. I was sure to leave grease on the chip top, but I 
> don't really know how much there should be.

The standard thermal greases conduct heat well, but not electricity
(high-conductivity silver-based ones *do* conduct electricity), so that
shouldn't be a problem.

>From your description though, you poked two holes in the packet and then
placed the entire packet between heat sink and processor?

I'm in contact with gamers who tend to go for excessive cooling, but I'm
fairly sure the proper procedure would be to poke one hole in the packet,
so you can direct the flow as you squeeze the thermal grease *directly*
onto the processor. Also you don't want an excessive layer of grease, as
though it conducts heat fairly well, it isn't nearly as good as the heat
sink material.

A Z80, sweet!  I had a Timex Sinclair 1000 back in '85 or '86.  I had to
remove the board from the case because it overheated.  The bridge
rectifier was screwed onto a flat aluminum square of metal that served
as the heat sink.  The CPU, a Z80-A running at 4MHz, did not require
any cooling infrastructure.  The overheating symptoms (sudden crash and
wispy) must have been a result of power failure, like maybe the
rectifier's semiconductor material stopped semiconducting at too high a
temp.  Is an overheating power supply still a feasible issue today?

Carlos Konstanski

From renegadepenguin at comcast.net  Fri Sep 22 22:41:13 2006
From: renegadepenguin at comcast.net (Renegade Penguin)
Date: Fri, 22 Sep 2006 22:41:13 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Newly assembled machine overheating
In-Reply-To: <4514C3DB.5050107@comcast.net>
References: <4514688F.60405@comcast.net>	<20060923031746.GA14083@gate.kl-ic.com>
	<4514C3DB.5050107@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <4514C8F9.2050208@comcast.net>

Okay - a couple of suggestions:

1) Only use the white thermal grease - NOT the silver stuff EVER.
2) Don't use too much.  Just a large drop is often enough.  The heat 
sink should be doing its job, not mostly the grease.
3) If it runs fine with the case side off, your problem is definitely 
100% airflow.
4) If you've got room for an additional case fan (or two) - use them.  
They're the inexpensive part of a system and as it gets older, you'll 
need better airflow.
5) Check cabling to see if you can minimize size - cables in the way of 
airflow will SERIOIUSLY overheat a small case.  Optional - switch to a 
mid or full tower with quad fans instead of a mini case.
6) Heat rises.  Make sure that the fans are the following:
    a) Front fan at BOTTOM - sucks in
    b) Back fan towards TOP - blows out
    c) POWER SUPPLY fan blows OUT.
    e) If there are two fans in the power supply, front or bottom fan 
sucks in, back fan blows out
7) If you've got a side-mount case fan (on the case side) - make sure 
it's working properly as well.  Lower half mounted - sucks in - upper 
half - blows out
8) Remove all the grease from proc & heat sink, start over with a large 
drop of grease (not a small blob)
9) If you have an aluminium only heat sink, switch to copper.  They're 
cheap compared to a full system.
10) Set the fans to run full speed

By the way, I have a 17" widescreen notebook with a 3 gigahertz desktop 
processor installed.  I have active cooling - a full-size 120 mm case 
fan installed directly below that blows air up into the chassis under 
the air intake - system blows HOT air out the back.  I lowered the 
temperature on my notebook (desktop replacement) by about 15C.  Purrs 
like a kitten.  It's got 3 onboard fans NORMALLY (case, video, proc) and 
still runs hot (they all do) without the active cooling.

Hope any of these are useful for you.

RP

# from Richard C. Steffens

>>Or the heat sink isn't properly anchored. ?
>
>Anything's possible, but it appears that it's really hard to have this
>thing look like it's anchored when it isn't. It was quite a struggle
>getting it on, but once it snapped into place it looked pretty secure.

Is it properly aligned?  IIRC, those sometimes go on only one way and 
leave a gap if you get them 180'd on accident.

As for airflow, the "case cover off" story makes me suspect 
short-circuiting.  Do you have an antec or similarly-incompetent case 
by any chance?  There should be no holes without a fan attached to 
them.  If there are, try packing tape.  Remember, you cannot make 
coolth, only remove warmth.

From rsteff at comcast.net  Sat Sep 23 14:35:39 2006
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Sat, 23 Sep 2006 14:35:39 -0700
Subject: Resolved: [PLUG] Newly assembled machine overheating
In-Reply-To: <4514C3DB.5050107@comcast.net>
References: <4514688F.60405@comcast.net>	<20060923031746.GA14083@gate.kl-ic.com>
	<4514C3DB.5050107@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <4515A8AB.8020001@comcast.net>

Thank you to all who offered ideas about what could be causing the Anti 
Burn Regulator alarm to sound on my mother board. It appears that the 
problem was the grease. When I removed the heat sink there was no grease 
on the chip, and there was an empty rectangle about the size of the chip 
surrounded by grease on the underside of the heat sink. There was also 
grease all around the chip on its carrier board.

I wiped off the heat sink and the excess around the chip on its board. I 
applied a modest amount of grease to the chip and re-installed the heat 
sink. Then, confident that I had solved the problem, I reinstalled the 
side of the case. The machine has been powered up for about 20 minutes 
and hasn't complained. Of course, the machine isn't doing much right 
now, but that's for the next thread.

Thanks again for all the help.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens

Keith Lofstrom wrote:

>Or the processor voltage is too high
>(check the BIOS for voltages, compare that to the processor type you
>have).
>  
>
There is a BIOS page with voltage select for CPU, DDR, and AGP. All 
three are set to Default.

Actual voltages are listed on the same BIOS page that list CPU 
temperatures. There are six voltages listed:
                         Actual
Vcore               1.64V
+3.3V               3.23V
+   5V               4.83V
+  12V             12.22V
DDR Voltage      2.48V
AGP Voltage      1.48V

A chart for the Athlon XP series shows 1.65V for Vcore, but I didn't 
find anything else about voltage.

>Some motherboards have all sorts of controls over fan speed in the BIOS.
>Record the current fan settings (so you can restore them), then set the
>fans to "high speed all the time".  If they still move slowly, that is
>one problem, if they move fast but the chip still gets hot, then it
>is probably the heat sink interface, or something not working.
>  
>
I didn't find anything other than FOC (Fan-Off Control), which may be 
Enabled or Disabled. The 'Item Help' says, "If enabled, this function 
protect user's CPU from overheating in an event there's a problem with 
the CPUFAN. The user should also plug the CPUFAN power on the CPUFAN1 
pin. If not, system will auto shutdown." I have FOC Enabled and the fan 
connected to CPUFAN1. CPUFAN2 does not connect the sensor line to the 
fan. I think that means it can't tell how fast the fan is running, and 
just runs full speed. I can try that, but the fan RPM only varies 
between 2721 and  2766 RPM (with the case side off).

I'll be trying to boot Knoppix shortly. If I can find a way to read the 
CPU Temp quickly before shutting down (is that something /proc keeps?), 
I'll try to check it. Right now it's running at 46 deg C/ 114 deg F.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens



From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Sat Sep 23 17:04:04 2006
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Sat, 23 Sep 2006 18:04:04 -0600 (MDT)
Subject: Not Resolved: [PLUG] Newly assembled machine overheating
In-Reply-To: <4515C8B7.2090904@comcast.net>
References: <4514688F.60405@comcast.net>
	<20060923031746.GA14083@gate.kl-ic.com>
	<4515C8B7.2090904@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0609231800520.10493@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

I used to use this script to poweroff a laptop once the CPU temp dips to
49 degrees Celsius.

Carlos Konstanski



#!/usr/bin/perl

#
# Shuts down the computer as soon as the temperature of the CPU drops to
# 49 degrees Celsius.  Requires acpi.
#
my $temp = 9999;

while($temp > 50) {
     $temp = `acpi -Bt \|grep -o -E \"\\w\\w\\.\\w\"`;
     print "Temperature is: $temp";
     sleep(3);
}

print "Powering off...\n";
system("/sbin/poweroff");
exit 0;

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Sun Sep 24 13:42:42 2006
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)

On Sun, 24 Sep 2006, RA Cowger wrote:

> Everything I have shows how to send ASCII codes to standard output, the
> screen, from the shell. I want to change fonts in my printer so I need to
> be able to send the code first, then I can send the file.

   How about redirection? Echo what you want to the screen, but add '> lpr'
(without the quotes) to redirect the output. You can also use the pipe
command '|' to send the display to lpr.

I tried a little experiment:

root at ns:/dev# echo "I rule" >/dev/lp0 
The printer sprang to life and did stuff, though it sadly did not print
anything.  But this was an overly simplistic test.  Redirecting the
output to the parallel port is probably the equivalent of the DOS (or
old-scool BASIC) LPRINT command.  If I had an old dot-matrix printer, I
might have actually seen some output, who knows?

Carlos Konstanski

>    Cue the theme from "The Twilight Zone." Today my Sony Vaio started acting

Fixed the problem as then your normal user could run commands, or then
root could run commands?

> Then it happened again,
> after I installed an application and tried to run it.

Run as who? (root or normal user?)

>
>    What might cause this behavior?

Screwing with your $PATH will do that.  Are you sure you didn't run
'rm -f g *'? (note the space before the *) That would toast your .
files, which would almost certainly have some effect on your PATH, but
no one elses. (it also wouldn't take effect until you opened a new
terminal, vt, or logged out / in.

Are you missing any files in your home dir?

Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0609241815180.10493@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

root's $PATH is different from that of a normal user.  Don't know which
distro you are using, or I would be able to tell you where each $PATH is
defined.

Does the full path, /usr/bin/rm, work for a normal user?  If so, then
the $PATH is broken.  echo $PATH to check it.  If it looks right, that's
when things get weird.

Check aliases to make sure an rm-overriding alias didn't get created.

Carlos Konstanski

From daniel at digitree.org  Sun Sep 24 19:53:32 2006
From: daniel at digitree.org (Daniel Hedlund)
Date: Sun, 24 Sep 2006 19:53:32 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Modifying LC_TIME
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0609241810230.3745@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0609241655080.3745@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>	<45172706.80900@digitree.org>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0609241810230.3745@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <451744AC.1090902@digitree.org>

Rich,

Rich Shepard wrote:
>   The problem is GTK+2 related, and was created somewhere between 2.6.10 
> and
> 2.8.12. Others experienced the same problem, but I don't recall the
> distributions they used. The issue affects all GTK+2 applications. I got
> caught when I had to upgrade the library as part of installing freerock
> gnome just so I can run gnucash. I stumble on dates because jpilot was 
> where
> I first experienced the difference and I refer to its calendar frequently
> during the day.

I've done a bit of testing and I've figured out what the GTK/GNOME 
settings are tied to.  It's specifically tied to root's locale settings 
(root's the LANG and LC_TIME variables).  This is because the X server 
is initially started as root, even if "startx" is run by the user. 
GNOME has no way of getting a user's individual locale settings because 
they're almost always set by a shell login script (ie. ~/.bashrc). 
There is no set standard location to keep this information that GNOME 
can rely on.

With that said, merely adding a line or two in the /root/.bashrc or 
another similar shell initialization script won't do the trick.  This is 
because X doesn't get started after logging in as root, it's usually 
done at the system level and doesn't pick up those variables.

The way to fix the problem is simply to define the LANG and/or LC_TIME 
variables in a system startup script that is high up in the execution 
chain, preferably somewhere like the rc.sysinit file(? - there may be 
better places to put the LANG info):
LANG="en_US.UTF-8"

What day of the week has the GNOME calendar been starting for you?  If 
it's been starting on a Saturday, then it's because the default locale 
was set to "" or "C", which picks up the "POSIX" LC_TIME info that says 
to start on a Saturday.  I was having the problem of starting on a 
Saturday because I set my system-wide LANG to "C" so that commands like 
'ls' wouldn't do stuff like mix upper, lowercase and ".*" files 
together.  This is what messed things up for me.  I found out that I 
could use a normal locale and still get sorting working properly by 
setting the LC_COLLATE variable to "POSIX" after setting the locale to 
what I wanted:
export LANG="en_US.UTF-8"
export LC_COLLATE="POSIX"

Cheers,

Daniel Hedlund
daniel at digitree.org
