>      object file: No such file or directory
>
> So far I've determined I
>   can't switch to a console screen and login,
>   can't run yum to install the missing package with libpam.so.0
>   can't symlink libpam.so to libpam.so.0 in /usr/lib
>   wish the knoppix disk wasn't at work
>
> "don't like" is a very mild expression of my yum attachment at the moment.
>

What did you do?  Yum breaking things is like that is pretty rare. In
fact, yum tends to have the opposite problem of not doing advanced
stuff and bailing when there are potential problems.

What does "rpm -q pam" show?  Can you install the pam RPM with rpm?
If you need to, you can use an HTTP URL with rpm (this is for FC5).

rpm -Uvh http://download.fedora.redhat.com/pub/fedora/linux/core/5/5/i386/os/Fedora/RPMS/pam-0.99.3.0-2.i386.rpm

Assuming that you can login as root. One thing to try is booting into
single user mode. PAM is one of those things which when it gets hosed
can be hard to fix internally.  Otherwise, you will need to boot off
the rescue CD.

 - Ian


From rich at paranoid.org  Thu Sep 28 15:14:09 2006
From: rich at paranoid.org (Rich Burroughs)
Date: Thu, 28 Sep 2006 15:14:09 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] I took a shot this morning
In-Reply-To: <451C3469.4080306@verizon.net>
References: <451C1E0E.8000904@verizon.net> <86mz8j232d.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
	<451C3469.4080306@verizon.net>
Message-ID: <17150.70.57.126.130.1159481649.squirrel@o4.hostbaby.com>

Bruce,

Someone trying to connect to a port is not necessarily evidence of
wrongdoing. That could happen for innocent reasons, like mistyping an IP
address.

Chances are, though, that it was someone scanning for a specific
vulnerability with a program that tends to run on that port. I'm not
positive, but I think that number is in the range used for RPC services.

There are programs that can scan large blocks of IP addresses, and look
for specific vulnerabilities. If the scan gets some hits, then an attacker
can try to exploit them later (or the scanning software might even try the
exploit itself).

Anyway, it's up to you how serious you want to take this, but I would
personally not be concerned. There's a lot of this kind of scanning that
happens. If you are going to file an abuse report every time someone hits
a port on your firewall, you are probably going to file a lot of reports.
I would be more concerned about someone who was trying to DoS me, or made
multiple, more persistent attempts to attack me.


Rich

You give them the right when you sign the agreement.  You also tell them 
that you will let them change the user agreement at any time, and that 
you agree to never ever take them to court and that you will pay the 
cost of the mediator that would hear your complaint.  You will not run a 
"server" of any kind...including ssh.  You agree to pay more if you hook 
up more than one computer.  Heck you even give them the right to give 
your personal info to companies and entities that they "do business" with.

Read the user agreement.  It is quite interesting.

maybe Fedora or whatever is like that.

From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Fri Sep 29 09:34:09 2006
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)
Date: Fri, 29 Sep 2006 09:34:09 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] VMWARE
In-Reply-To: <c834ec80609290908u2ec00cbn3768737a7ffbd893@mail.gmail.com>
References: <1159542666.451d378aaa69b@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
	<c834ec80609290908u2ec00cbn3768737a7ffbd893@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <1159547649.3413.16.camel@willow.odshp.com>

On Fri, 2006-09-29 at 09:08 -0700, Rogan Creswick wrote:
> On 9/29/06, plug_0 at robinson-west.com <plug_0 at robinson-west.com> wrote:
> > I get the following error after installing kernel-devel via yum and
> > trying to run vmware-config.pl...
> 
> I don't know YUM based distros at all, but isn't there a
> kernel-headers package you could install rather than the kernel dev
> package?  IIRC, if you use a full kernel tree, you need to at least
> configure it to the same config as your running kernel.
> 
> FWIW, I don't believe I've ever seen *kernel headers (when installed
> separate from the whole src tree)* installed to /usr/src/linux.  But
> maybe Fedora or whatever is like that.

kernel-devel is the kernel headers package, but it installed
in /usr/src/kernels/$(uname -r)-$(uname -p)/.  By
convention, /lib/modules/$(uname -r)/build is a symlink to kernel
headers, which is where vmware-config.pl looks and then
suggests /usr/src/linux if it fails, since that's conventional.

Wil

Wil Cooley <wcooley at nakedape.cc>
http://nakedape.cc

It is useful to test a running firewall.  Send your IP address to a
friend (for heaven sakes don't post it to the list) who can run nmap
against it.  The firewall prevent abuse from happening, but it is 
good to test it.

That said, as the Internet "matures" - that is, sinks towards senility -
it is loaded with millions of infected machines spewing their little
zombied brains out, rattling every internet address in sight.  If
packets were bullets, you would move to Mogadishu or Bagdhad to get
away from the carnage.  My IP addresses get thousands of such attempts
per day, and my firewall is set to blow off most of them and not even
log them.  I just log the open ports so I can see stuff that actually
should make it through that doesn't.

Oh well.  If computer software was free, and companies like Microsoft
had to find revenue through support sales rather than product sales,
computer viruses would be as common as bystanders getting hit by
parts from exploding Zeppelins.   Oh, the humanity ...

Keith

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Fri Sep 29 11:02:12 2006
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Fri, 29 Sep 2006 12:02:12 -0600 (MDT)
Subject: [PLUG] VMWARE
In-Reply-To: <ca5165530609290935x418587e1l6c313be24827434e@mail.gmail.com>
References: <1159542666.451d378aaa69b@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
	<ca5165530609290935x418587e1l6c313be24827434e@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0609291157560.4215@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

I just had to deal with a similar issue with an Acronis install on
Fedora.  I fixed it by re-installing the kernel and kernel-devel
packages and rebooting.  The existing /lib/modules/<uname -r>/build
symlink was pointing at a non-existant location.  In other words, the
modules and the headers were out of sync.  Hence the re-install, which
fixed it.

There is another problem you are likely to have with vmware-config.pl.
If the kernel was compiled with a version of gcc that differs from your
gcc version, the install will fail.  The best remedy is to build your
own custom kernel.  Incidentally, building your own kernel also solves
the problem you are having right now.

Distro kernels blow.

Carlos Konstanski

From daniel at digitree.org  Fri Sep 29 12:12:05 2006
From: daniel at digitree.org (Daniel Hedlund)
Date: Fri, 29 Sep 2006 12:12:05 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] VMWARE
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0609290906380.28602@blackbox.fnordora.org>
References: <1159542666.451d378aaa69b@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0609290906380.28602@blackbox.fnordora.org>
Message-ID: <451D7005.5040800@digitree.org>

alan wrote:
> You need to get the patched version of the vmware kernel modules.  
> Search for "vmware-tools-any-update1".

Isn't that supposed to be the 'vmware-any-any' patch?  I believe it 
fixes a lot of problems with VMWare on newer Linux distros.  It's a good 
idea to apply this patch regardless of whether you need it or not; at a 
minimum I think it fixes some memory issues and problems with hanging 
when a computer is shut down.
http://ftp.cvut.cz/vmware/

About the original poster's issue with the address space size, there is 
the possibility that your package manager has a newer kernel available 
than the one you are running.  Package managers tend to download kernel 
headers for the newest kernel, which might not be the same version as 
what you're running.  If you've upgraded your kernel at some point and 
not sure that you are running the latest version, you could just try 
restarting as well.  Yes, there are more complex ways of finding out, 
but restarting is probably the easiest if the newest kernel is always 
loaded by default.

Cheers,

Daniel Hedlund
daniel at digitree.org

	Moon patiently told the student the following story -- "One day a
student came to Moon and said, "I understand how to make a better garbage
collector..."

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Sat Sep 30 19:05:29 2006
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Sat, 30 Sep 2006 20:05:29 -0600 (MDT)
Subject: [PLUG] VMware Install on SuSE
In-Reply-To: <451F1AFD.6020009@comcast.net>
References: <451F1AFD.6020009@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0609301937490.8203@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

libdb is part of the "db" package.  Look for "db" in YaST.  This is the
Berkeley DB Database.  It would be weird if you didn't already have db
because RPM uses it.  The more likely scenario is that your version is
too old.

See http://rpmfind.net/linux/RPM/suse/9.3/i386/suse/i686/db-4.3.27-3.1.i686.html

I realize this is a URL to a 9.3 repository, and you have 10.1.  As long
as the package version is good enough, I'm not sure that matters.

Carlos Konstanski
